Investigation of Flood Damage in Hunan Province Counties 73

Divided into Four Groups for Departure

Relief to be Implemented Immediately After Investigation

Changsha Correspondence: This year's flood in Hunan Province is severe, affecting fifty-four counties, accounting for more than two-thirds of the province's area. The losses are incalculable. The Central Government has specially dispatched Zhou Yi Kui, a commissioner to Hunan to investigate the flood, along with engineers Chen Zong Xiang, and inspection committee members Zhou Xi Cheng, Zhang Fu Yin, Cheng Zhen Ze, and Zhang Ying Xi, etc., arrived in the province on the 27th. In recent days, they have convened joint meetings at the Provincial Relief Headquarters with representatives from the Civil Affairs and Construction Bureaus, resolving the following matters regarding the flood investigation: (A) The inspection area will only select counties with more severe disasters, dividing them into four groups for investigation as follows: (1) The first group consists of eleven counties: Nanxian, Hanshou, Yuanjiang, Changde, Huarong, Lixian, Yiyang, Xiangyin, Yueyang, Linxiang, and Anxiang, plus Jinggang City. (2) The second group consists of seven counties: Hengshan, Hengyang, Qiyang, Dongan, Linli, Shimen, and Cili. (3) The third group consists of six counties: Xiangxiang, Shaoyang, Xupu, Xinhua, Anhua, and Xiangtan. (4) The fourth group consists of four counties: Taoyuan, Yuanling, Luxi, and Chenxi. The remaining counties, due to inconvenient transportation, cannot be thoroughly inspected and will only be investigated by personnel dispatched by the Provincial Relief Headquarters. (B) Committee Assignments: First Group: Central Government – Zhou Yi Kui, Chen Zong Xiang; Civil Affairs Bureau – Lian Bi Shan; Construction Bureau – Cao Zong Hai; Provincial Relief Headquarters – Peng Mao Yuan. Second Group: Central Government – Cheng Zhen Ze; Construction Bureau – Xie Huai Zhen; Provincial Relief Headquarters – Tang Zheng Heng. Third Group: Central Government – Zhang Fu Yin; Construction Bureau – Zhou Feng Jiu; Provincial Relief Headquarters – Liu Ju An. Fourth Group: Central Government – Zhou Xi Cheng; Construction Bureau – Wang Hui Xian; Provincial Relief Headquarters – Jiang Xiao Fan. (C) Departure Dates for Investigation: The first group is scheduled to depart on the 31st; the second, third, and fourth groups are scheduled to depart on the 30th. (D) Inspection Considerations: (1) The affected area will be calculated in square kilometers. (2) The causes of the flood, such as lake and river overflows, flash floods, and excessive water accumulation in low-lying areas. (3) The current number of affected people. (4) The number of people displaced by the disaster and their living conditions. (5) The number of deaths among the affected people. (6) Losses of houses and property, converted to yuan. (7) The number of acres of farmland flooded and the percentage of reduced yield. (8) When harvests are poor, how many more people will be affected by the disaster. (9) According to the climate, is it possible to replant other types of grain. (10) Which is more convenient, distributing grain or providing cash relief. (11) Has the local area implemented self-relief measures, and what are the methods. (Note: Quantity of grain and money, and number of people). (12) Number of people awaiting relief. (13) The rise and fall of grain prices, calculated by the value per catty, divided into large wheat, millet, sorghum, corn, and other product names, and divided into conditions before and after the flood. (E) Disaster material from each county will be collected by the Provincial Relief Headquarters. All disaster area pictures, cameras, and other items necessary for the investigation should be compiled and handed over to each group of committee members for their use by the Provincial Relief Headquarters. After the above items were decided, the provincial government telegraphed all counties, ordering them to properly receive and protect the inspection personnel. He Jian of the First Group also invited the Director of the Civil Affairs Bureau, Cao Bo Wen, the President of the High Court, Chen Chang Cu, and members of the Provincial Government, Wu Jian Xue, etc., to participate in the investigation, scheduled to go to Yuanjiang, Hanshou, and Nanxian first, and planned to return to the province within three or four days. All duties as Commander-in-Chief of the Fourth Route have been delegated to Chief of Staff Liu Ying Gu. The duties of the Chairman of the Provincial Government have been delegated to Cao Dian Qiu. Accompanying He Jian on his departure were two secretaries, aides-de-camp, military doctors, and quartermasters each, and a company of guards, traveling on two armored motorboats, also carrying medicines for immediate distribution. It is reported that after the committee members of each group have completed their inspections and returned to the province, a relief strategy will be determined. (August 30)

Zhang Fang Appeals for Henan Flood Victims 74

Zhang Fang, Chairman of the Henan Provincial Relief Committee, telegraphed on the East River to: Chiang, Chairman of the Nanjing National Government; Zhang, Deputy Commander of the Shenyang Army, Navy, and Air Force; Song, Chairman of the Shanghai Fundraising Committee for Urgent Relief for Provincial Floods; Presidents of various academies and ministers of various departments in Nanjing; Xu, Chairman of the Relief Committee; various provincial governments, provincial relief committees, charitable organizations, and newspaper offices. Respectfully, the province of Henan has suffered from continuous rain, causing rivers to overflow. The flooded area has exceeded half of the province. Here are the essential details of each county's disaster situation, urgently requesting rescue and relief. It is now reported by the Fangcheng County Relief Subcommittee and various district chiefs that since the beginning of summer this year, two months of continuous rain have turned the plains into a swamp. By the end of June and the beginning of July, even more heavy rain fell continuously, day and night. The city walls collapsed for more than thirty feet, and the river water overflowed. The Pan River and Jia River to the east of the city, and the Fu River and Zhao River to the west of the city, burst and flowed horizontally, unable to be stopped. In the Heiyan Zhuang area in the east district and the Wang Tu Zhuang villages in the west district, fields were washed into ditches, and people and livestock drifted with the water. Right at that moment, it was late at night, and many people were crushed and killed by collapsed houses, or drowned immediately. It is estimated that more than 17,000 houses collapsed, and more than 630 civilians died. The Fanshui County Relief Subcommittee reported that this year's wheat harvest was poor, and autumn crops were being planted when they were initially hit by severe drought, followed by continuous rain. By July and August, heavy rain fell repeatedly, and the autumn seedlings on both banks of the Si River were completely submerged. The Yellow River's water was surging, and both new and old beach areas were covered with silt. It is estimated that more than 600 hectares of farmland in the southern mountain areas were washed into ditches, and the number of collapsed houses is even harder to count. The Pingdeng County Relief Subcommittee reported that on the 8th and 10th of August, heavy rain fell for eleven days and nights. The Yi River suddenly rose, reaching from Jiu Gao in the south to Longmen in the north, covering dozens of miles in the east and west, with no boundaries. The people were in dire straits, mulberry fields became a sea, and the exact number of losses and refugees is currently under investigation. The Yiyang County Party Department reported that in recent years, the people have suffered from soldiers, bandits, drought, and locusts. Without anticipating that the wounds were still present, floods have occurred again. Since the beginning of summer this year, prolonged rain has not stopped. In early July, torrential rain poured down, turning highlands and plains into a vast expanse of water. The sound of collapsing houses never ceased, and belongings and livestock were all swept away. An investigation of the Lian Zhuang Li Canal Sun Liu Han Cheng Liu Quan Shui Que areas north and south of the Luo River, as well as the Shui Po Tou and other villages in the county seat, covering an area of less than a hundred li, revealed that no less than several thousand houses had collapsed and several thousand acres of farmland had been washed away. The extent of other losses can be imagined. The Weishi County Relief Subcommittee reported that since June, there had been continuous rain for weeks without stopping. Low-lying fields and crops were already submerged. By early August, heavy rain poured down, flooding mountains and hills, and the autumn crops were completely submerged. The new and old Jia Lu Rivers and Shuang Ji Rivers burst their banks, and overflowed wildly. Not only were the fields and crops lost, but all the houses were washed away, and many people and livestock were crushed and killed. There is no hope for the autumn harvest. The Jiaxian County Relief Subcommittee reported that due to frequent banditry, nine out of ten houses were empty. This spring, the troops suppressed the bandits, and the residents began to feel slightly at ease. Who would have thought that since the beginning of summer, months of continuous rain had made any harvest impossible. On the evening of August 10th, torrential rain fell again, not stopping all night. Mountain floods surged, and the Ru River overflowed, flooding dozens of villages along the river. Possessions and food were all gone, and there was no place to live. The water was about four or five feet deep, and approximately hundreds of people died. Representatives of the people from the second district of Lanfeng County presented a report stating that this district is located near the Yellow River, with land level with the water. Every time there is a rise, it overflows. This year, when the ice thawed in the spring river, the water flowed horizontally and vertically, and the wheat seedlings were submerged, already causing unbearable suffering. By the end of July and the beginning of August, there was continuous heavy rain for half a month without stopping. The water was five or six feet deep on the plains, submerging autumn crops, collapsing houses, and washing away countless people and livestock. The Civil Affairs Department forwarded a report from the magistrate of Minquan County, relayed by representatives of the people from the first, second, and third districts, stating that last year's war disasters had left the area in ruins. Who knew that human disasters had just ended when natural disasters struck again. Since the beginning of summer, continuous rain has been a scourge, with water several feet deep, collapsing houses, casualties among people and livestock, and all the autumn crops submerged. The affected people have nowhere to eat or sleep. The Civil Affairs Department forwarded a report from the village chiefs of various villages in the second and fifth districts of Anyang County, stating that the district has a Guangrun Lake that is shaped like the bottom of a pot. It has always accumulated water when flooded and never dries up throughout the year. This month, in August, the Caiyuan Town in Tangyin County, which belongs to the south of the lake, experienced a flash flood in the Tang River, which was very turbulent. The waves rolled and all flowed into the lake, causing dozens of villages to turn into swamps. Currently, there has been continuous rain for a long time, submerging all the autumn crops, making it difficult to sow wheat, and causing severe spring famine. These situations have all been reported to the meeting. An investigation has revealed that there are now sixty-seven counties in Henan Province affected by the flood. The number of distressed people is estimated to be over fifteen million. Relief will bring life, while no relief will bring death. It is hoped that the central government and charitable groups everywhere will quickly provide generous assistance to save these people. The telegram cannot fully express the anticipation of waiting for orders. One.

The Yalu River Also Suffers from Major Flooding 75

Counties such as Andong and Linjiang are Submerged

Andong Correspondence: In the middle ten days of August, the upper and lower reaches of the Yalu River experienced a rise in water, with surging waves. At the time, merchants and residents along the river were all terrified. Not long after it receded, on the 26th and 27th, it was reported that there was a second rise in water, with the water level increasing more than before. This was because from 10 p.m. on the 25th to midnight on the 26th, torrential rain poured down without stopping. At the same time, counties along the upper reaches of the river also experienced the same torrential rain, causing the river to rise significantly. From 10 a.m. to 11 p.m. on the 27th, the water level was at its highest. Low-lying areas in the city and its suburbs, as well as the Hou Chao Gou area, were a vast expanse of water, turning into swamps. Among them, the water depth in Hou Chao Gou, the east end of Zhenan Bridge, and in front of the Shahe Town train station was three or four feet due to the proximity of the Dasha River, blocking transportation. Only a dozen small boats were traveling back and forth. Also, when the river water first rose on the morning of the 26th, the county government immediately dispatched the third section to supervise various section chiefs, clerks, and staff members, dividing them into groups to patrol the river embankments day and night, taking measures to prevent flooding. On the morning of the 27th, the county government received reports of rising water from counties along the upper reaches of the river. It was reported that the water had risen twelve feet in Linjiang County, seventeen feet in Waichagou, twenty-four feet in Changdianhekou, and twenty-one feet in Mashitai. On the morning of the 27th, more than a dozen sailboats and wooden rafts docked on the riverbank were washed away by the water. There were also forty-two timber workers from a certain lumberyard who were washed away, with their fate unknown. As of 9 a.m. on the 28th, according to measurements of the river's water level by the third section of the county government, it had only slightly receded by about three feet. The flooded areas in the city and Hou Chao Gou were still a vast expanse of water. The number of merchant and resident households affected by the flooding was about 250, with a total of 2,100 people. When the water surged on the 26th and 27th, merchants and residents in the area fled in droves. However, the general poor households had nowhere to go and were sleeping on the streets, crying out for food. Their situation was pitiful. The Andong County Office, in conjunction with the Commerce Bureau, the Public Security Bureau, and the General Chamber of Commerce, dispatched personnel on the afternoon of the 28th to take in refugees, temporarily using two large silk factories as temporary shelters. As of the afternoon of the 29th, a total of 725 men and women had been taken in. Following the previous method of providing relief to Korean refugees, they were provided with ample food to satisfy their hunger. The funds needed were allocated from the remaining 3,000 yuan from the previous relief effort. (August 30)

Zhu and Mao Gather Between Gan County and Wan'an 76

Reports from Various Armies of Defeating Large Groups of Red Bandits

Public Teachers Report Zhu De Seriously Injured

Nanchang Correspondence: Recent news from the front lines indicates that there are no traces of bandits to the north of a line extending from Guangchang, Nanfeng, Le'an, and Yongfeng in the east to Jishui and Ji'an in the west. Strong fortifications have been built in Ningdu and Xingguo to the south for defense. Currently, the left wing, in addition to a portion defending the fortifications and clearing out scattered bandits and peasant bandits, is pursuing bandits who fled south towards Xingguo. Originally, after Zhu and Mao gathered in Liantang, they fled south from Gaoqingxu, Chongxian, Longping, and Yongfengxu to the area between Gan County and Wan'an. Their fake Central Military Commission's rear hospital was located in the Luxu area (bordering Gan County, Wan'an, Yudu, and Xingguo), near Lirenkeng, planning to connect with Li Mingrui, who was entrenched south of Gan County, in Chongyi and Shangyou, and flee to the border areas of Jiangxi, Guangdong, and Hunan. Zhu De was injured in Ningdu and is currently being treated in Lirenkeng. Rumors say he was bombed to death. The following is a transcription of telegrams reporting victories from various armies: (A) Telegram from the Staff Office of the 28th Division on the 30th: (1) Bi's regiment departed from Taihe and destroyed bandit nests in Yongyang and Ruyang (bordering Ji'an) within a day, killing over thirty bandits and capturing over ten alive. (2) This afternoon, over a thousand bandits were discovered across the river along the creek. Yang's brigade concentrated artillery fire across the river, while the Minkuan warship used machine guns and airplanes bombed them, killing many bandits and scattering the rest. (3) Li's battalion in Wan'an, this morning, defeated a fake independent regiment in Henglu Zhongpo, at the border of the three counties of Xingguo, Taihe, and Tai'an, killing dozens of bandits, seizing many guns, and rescuing dozens of hostages. (B) Telegram from General Commander Jiang stating, "Today, I selected over three hundred brave soldiers and disguised them with captured bandit army armbands and flags, ordering them to search the bandit area of Qingxi Xikeng in groups of three to five, while the majority continued to follow. At 11:00, they reached the bandit area. The bandits recognized them as comrades, and officials from the fake Soviet governments of Xingguo and Ruijin came to welcome them. My troops immediately surrounded and fiercely attacked them. The bandit crowd scrambled to escape, capturing the chairman of the fake Ruijin government, one committee member, and one member of the fake Xingguo committee, all of whom were executed on the spot as a warning to the public. Over ninety bandits were killed. Also captured was a fake division commander of Zhu's bandit troops, Zhu Jianxun, who was injured in the Ningdu campaign and was receiving treatment here. He has been brought back to be interrogated to obtain information about the bandit army's situation." (C) Telegram from Zhao Yong, a subordinate of Public Teacher Commander, on the 31st, stating, "There are many wounded bandits in Lirenkeng, between Taihe and Gan County. The bandit leader Zhu De is still injured and is being treated here. Zhu's guard regiment, after a long period of recruitment, now has over a thousand men serving as guards here. Yesterday, they were bombed by our airplanes, causing many casualties and deaths. They fled to Bailu and Gaoqiao overnight, abandoning approximately two thousand wounded and sick bandits." (September 1)

Wu Peifu Passes Through Chengdu to Songpan 77

Will Take the Road Through Longnan Out of Sichuan

Chengdu Correspondence: Wu Peifu arrived in Chengdu from Tongchuan the other day, passing through Guanghan County to Xindu County, forty li from Chengdu, on July 12th. He stayed in Baoguang Temple, a famous temple in the county, and visited Gui Lake, which is the site of the former residence of Yang Shengan, the Ming Dynasty minister. On the 16th, he took a car sent by the province to welcome him to the province. On the day of his arrival in the province, the entire city of Chengdu hung flags to welcome him. In the morning, troops from the 28th, 29th, and 24th Army headquarters were dispatched to welcome him at Sima Bridge outside the North Gate. Officials from various agencies who arrived included the two army commanders Deng and Tian. At 12:00, Wu's car arrived in the province. Military music played, and the troops presented arms. Wu got out of the car and nodded to the two army commanders and other welcomers one by one, with a smile on his face. He was wearing a Tai straw hat, a gray silk long gown, and a black gauze vest. His beard and hair were mostly white, his face was yellowish-black and slightly thin, and he was fifty-eight years old. He spoke with a Shandong accent. After sitting in the reception room for a while, he rode a large black horse prepared by Army Commander Deng into the city, accompanied by more than twenty guards, each carrying a handgun. He was led by the adjutant of the 28th Army on horseback, passing through North Main Street, Gulou Street, Tidu East Street, and Shuwa Street to the former Foreign Affairs Office residence. In the afternoon, he left the North Gate with his guards and resided in Zhaojue Temple. The hundreds of guards who came with Wu also stayed at Zhaojue Temple. Along the way, those who wanted to see Wu's demeanor crowded the streets.

On the fifth day after Wu arrived in the province, Song Yunzi, the president of the Guoxue Association, sent a letter inviting him to lecture on the I Ching at the auditorium of Dacheng School, summoning members to listen. At 10:00 in the morning, Wu Zhicheng first announced the opening of the meeting, followed by Guan Menglan delivering a welcome speech, and then Wu lectured on the I Ching. His words were grand, using heavenly virtue, the way of the king, and sacred achievements as the outline, discussing the sequence of the Former Heaven and Later Heaven trigrams of Fu Xi and King Wen, and concluding with saving the country through the teachings of rites. However, he spoke in Shandong dialect, which most people did not understand. Approximately a thousand people attended that day, mostly from academic circles. What was particularly noteworthy was that the bodyguards Wu brought with him wore five-colored caps and did not change the insignia. It is unknown why he insisted on this.

On August 2nd, Wu set off from the province to Guanxian, ostensibly to escape the summer heat at Mount Qingcheng in Guanxian. However, he was hindered by rain after arriving in Guanxian and stayed in Guanxian City for five days. On the 7th, he traveled west, passing through Songpan to leave Sichuan. On the 9th, he passed through Wenchuan. It was not until the 13th that he reached Maoxian. According to a telegram from Maoxian, Wu set off for Songpan on the 16th. Since the Song-Guan Highway has been half completed, it is estimated that it will take seven days to arrive. It is said that after Wu arrives in Songpan, he will take the road through Longnan out of Sichuan. It is said that he has already sent Liu to Gansu because the Five Ma warlords of Gansu Army sent telegrams supporting Wu last year, hence his trip to Gansu. (August 17)

Local Correspondence

Songjiang 78

The Case of the Patrolmen Demanding Pay Reaches a Conclusion: The patrolmen from the four districts of the city and suburbs, because the police pay for July from the First District Office was delayed and their meals were not provided, went to the District Office together to demand their pay on the 29th of last month, causing a dispute. It is now known that the outstanding money was cleared on the 3rd. It is reported that after the District Chief reported the fact that the patrolmen demanded their pay to the County Government, he received instruction No. 964, which stated that the patrol officers of the four detachments led the patrolmen of each shift to the District Office to demand their pay. The patrol officers did not understand the system and acted without authorization, which was inappropriate. They have been reprimanded separately. The Director of the Public Security Bureau, who did not prevent this in advance, has also been given a warning punishment. The patrolmen of each shift have been ordered to be strictly restrained. As for the date of pay distribution by the District Office, it should be handled in accordance with the resolutions of the County Political Conference.

Danger of the Seawall: A Telegram Requesting Reinforcement: The County Chamber of Commerce convened a joint meeting of various trade associations on the 5th to raise donations for the flood disaster. It was unanimously resolved to raise a large sum in the shortest possible time and send it to the meeting for transfer. In view of the danger of the Jinshan Mouth seawall, it was further resolved to urgently telegraph the Construction Department of the Provincial Government. The message stated: "The Jinshan Mouth seawall has been destroyed again in this disaster. There are already breaches, and the danger is extremely urgent. We request that personnel be dispatched to supervise the work and block the breaches as soon as possible to protect lives." It is reported that Lu Zhidong, the Executive Member of the County, returned to Songjiang from Shanyang after his public business and personally saw the high tide. Over a thousand piles of wood in front were blown out, and the seawall had been destroyed in several places, making it extremely dangerous. He has appealed to the County Construction Bureau to quickly plan for a rainy day to protect people's lives.

Suzhou 79

Three Agencies Hold a Meeting to Investigate the Disaster Situation: This year's flood in Wu County has submerged over 300,000 acres of farmland, the severity of the disaster being unprecedented in twenty years. The township district offices have submitted requests to the county to exempt them from the grain tribute. Currently, the county government has organized a flood relief committee to handle the aftermath. Now, personnel have been dispatched by the County Government Finance Bureau and the County Farmers' Association, respectively, to depart on the 8th of this month to inspect the disaster situation in various affected areas.

Actively Developing Wu 30th May Road and Park Road: The Wu County Construction Bureau has received approval from the Construction Department to widen and rebuild 30th May Road and Park Road within the city and is urgently awaiting construction. The buildings that should be demolished on both sides of the two roads have long been announced and notified to be demolished and handed over within a time limit. Now that the time limit has passed, many owners are still hesitating, and the park, the Reformatory, the public sports field, etc., have not been handed over as required. As a result, the project cannot proceed. Yesterday (the 5th), Director Qian submitted a resolution to the Party and Government Talk Meeting that the houses obstructing the opening of the two roads should be demolished and handed over as required, and the public buildings in each of these places should take the lead in handing over to facilitate the project.

A Staff Member of the Rehabilitation Center Embezzles Funds and Flees: Wu Zhenglun, an assistant at the Jiangsu Rehabilitation Center, is in his early twenties. His father runs the Tongyihe Western Clothing Store on Pengpeng Road in Shanghai. Recently, he suddenly embezzled 515 yuan of public funds and fled. Yesterday (the 5th), the center sent a letter to the Detective Team, dispatching detectives to Shanghai to investigate and arrest him.

The Suspicious Death Case in Songjiang Will Be Re-Examined: In the case of the unclear death of the woman Hu Zhang in Songjiang County, an autopsy determined that she had committed suicide by hanging. The related parties, Hu Yinglong and Hu Hou, were declared innocent by the Wuxi County Court. The prosecutor did not agree and appealed to the High Court, sending Hu et al. along with nine packages of Hu Zhang's remains to Suzhou. Now, the High Court has sent the case back to the Wu County District Court for re-examination in order to be convincing.

Changshu 80

The Bandit Zheng Ming and His Mother Meet, Disturbing the Northeast Township of Changshu: The bandit Zheng Ming, who is rampant in the area of Changshu Northeast Township, has been more rampant in various harbors since his father, Zheng Yushan, was executed in connection with a case. The detective team of the local Public Security Bureau arrested Zheng Ming in Shanghai and escorted him back to Changshu. He has confessed and is imprisoned in jail. Zheng learned that when his father was about to be executed, he had a Han jade bracelet that was preserved by the county government. Zheng Ming requested that the bracelet be returned when the court was in session. The official instructed him that his mother must come to claim it. Zheng then wrote a letter to his mother, Pan, asking her to come to the city. She arrived on the 3rd to visit him in prison. The bandit Zheng said to his mother, "You and I only have this one meeting today. You don't have to be sad. It's not like you only gave birth to one son. You can go back now. My father's Han jade bracelet is currently stored in the county government. You can go and claim it." His mother was extremely saddened upon hearing this and could only leave in tears. Pan then went to the county government and requested that the jade bracelet be returned. After Shen Cheng, the investigating official, approved it, she was allowed to take it. It is reported that the bracelet is indeed Han jade and was most loved by Deng Yushan during his lifetime.

Request to Reduce the Business Tax Amount Denied: The business tax of this county is contracted by the County Chamber of Commerce's organizing committee to the Provincial Department for 50,000 yuan per year, to be paid in four installments. Unexpectedly, since the start of collection, the business tax assessed is only 30,000 yuan, which is far from sufficient. A meeting was convened with various trade associations, and although more was agreed to be recognized, it was still difficult to meet the amount. In the latter part of last month, committee member Zhang Shouyi went to the province to personally meet with Director Xu of the Finance Department, intending to request a reduction of 20,000 yuan. Director Xu then said that this business tax was a contract signed by the responsible persons of both parties, the Chamber of Commerce, and should be adhered to. It is difficult to make changes during the contract period. At most, the recognition period can be shortened to the end of the year (half a year). The autumn and winter installments should still be handled according to the contract. Committee member Zhang had no choice but to return dejectedly.

Wuxi 81

Tragic News of a Yarn Factory Mechanic Losing an Arm: Zhou Erda, a twenty-one-year-old mechanic in the fine yarn room of the Yukon Yarn Factory under the North Xin Bridge in the Zhou Shanbang area of this county, was on duty at around 6:00 PM the day before yesterday (the 4th). He used a bamboo ladder to climb onto the wheel and shaft to install the belt. Unfortunately, Zhou was careless, and his right arm was caught in the wheel and rotated with the belt. When Su Yunting, a mechanic from the same factory, caught sight of it, he immediately turned off the machine. However, Zhou's right arm had already been crushed by the wheel, his back of the head had been broken, and blood was flowing uncontrollably from his ear, leaving him completely unconscious, in a particularly tragic state. A female worker, Cai Xiaomei, thirteen years old, was watching nearby and was also hit in the head by the belt. Su Yunting immediately transported the two injured people to the Brothers Hospital for treatment. Cai Xiaomei's injuries were not serious, but Zhou Erda's injuries were very serious, and his life was feared to be in danger. The Court Establishes a Real Estate Registration Office: The County Court of this county announced yesterday that real estate registration is established to prove rights and prevent disputes. The law is good, the intention is beautiful, the profits are small, and the effects are great. At the beginning of the establishment of the court, the registration office could not be established at the same time. As a result, property rights lawsuits have been increasing daily. In order to ensure the property rights of the people and clarify the source of litigation, the Jiangsu Higher Court has forwarded a request to the Judicial Administration Department for approval to establish a real estate registration office. It was officially established on August 1st. In addition to reporting it, the benefits of registration and the precautions regarding registration are listed below for the public to know. For real estate rights that occurred before July 31st of this year, registration must be applied for at the registration office of this court before September 30th. For registrations that occur after August 1st, the first deadline is one month for declaring registration. For registrations that occur after the deadline or are ordered to be registered due to other matters, the registration fee will be doubled. All should comply, and do not delay and misunderstand.

Nantong 82

Tai County Disaster Victims Sent to Nantong for Accommodation: The Provincial Relief Affairs Committee telegraphed the county government, stating that Tai County disaster victims were rescued from danger and sent to Nantong for accommodation. County Magistrate Zhang immediately dispatched personnel to locate the Falun Temple and Guichi Guild Hall as shelters. The Jiangbei Flood Relief Temporary Charity Association telegraphed the county government on the 4th, reporting that the flood in Yancheng was severe, requiring urgent relief, especially boats. The county government has telegraphed various districts to seal and hire boats to be sent to the city for use.

Nantong's Disaster Relief Situation: The Nantong County Government telegraphed the provincial government on the 4th, reporting on the disaster relief efforts, stating that the relief personnel were now divided into groups and dispatched. The first group consisted of two tugboats, two tugboats, twenty civilian boats, one thousand bags of flour, and eight thousand pieces of dry food, departing from Nantong on the 29th. They arrived in Dongtai on the 1st and went to Xinghua on the 2nd. The second group consisted of two tugboats, three tugboats, twenty-two civilian boats, two hundred bags of flour, and seven thousand pieces of dry food, departing on the 2nd, gathering in Anfeng, and going to Xingdong. Preparations are still underway, but there is a severe shortage of funds for the boats, causing great difficulty. Regarding the establishment of shelters, the association has already located sites.

Yangzhou 83

Yangzhong Suffers a Major Flood, Requests Urgent Relief: On the 26th of last month, around 3 AM, Yangzhong experienced strong winds and heavy rain, with a sudden surge in the river tide, causing the dikes to collapse and the banks to be breached. Villages and streets were submerged in water, almost leading to a catastrophe. Although the river tide has receded in the county, the breached dikes are still flooded. More than a hundred collapsed embankments inland have been hastily repaired, but the river dikes cannot be constructed due to the large scale of the work and the enormous cost. With the cool autumn approaching, the 30,000 to 40,000 disaster victims without clothing or food will be in dire straits. However, the county is barren and the people are poor, lacking wealthy merchants and households. There is no way to provide urgent relief. County Magistrate Bi has telegraphed the provincial government and various departments, appealing for urgent relief. The original telegram is recorded below: (Official titles omitted) Greetings. The Yangzhong flood caused the dikes to break, houses to collapse, and people to drown. The disaster victims gathered in crowds and made noise, almost causing trouble. I have repeatedly telegraphed, requesting you to send personnel to survey the area and issue urgent relief. Although the disaster situation may not be the most severe in the province, it is unprecedented in Yangzhong. The disaster victims are crying out for food and are easily emotionally agitated. The able-bodied men are working day and night, and it is difficult to ensure that they will not complain after prolonged labor. Although the county magistrate has done his best to appease them with sincerity, there is little practical benefit for the people. Therefore, I appeal again for prompt allocation of urgent relief and dispatch of personnel to survey and implement relief measures, to show that the county magistrate's appeal is not false, and to demonstrate that relief and rescue are not hopeless. Knowing that the provincial funds are stretched and difficult to allocate, if the need for relief can be met, the people's hearts can be calmed, and it will be easier to work for the aftermath. I submit this telegram with fear and trembling, expressing the utmost urgency.

Ningbo 84

Suspected Bandit Zhang Rizhong Apprehended: Li Xibai, a resident of Baitu Town, Fenghua, is currently working in the First Bandit Suppression Propaganda Department of the Nanjing General Headquarters. His father, Li Zunying, was at home when six or seven bandits suddenly came in early May of this year, kidnapped Li's father. Afterwards, his family repeatedly sent people to negotiate the ransom with the bandits, but the bandits, unable to get the price they demanded, tore up the ticket of Li's father last month. After Li heard the news in Nanjing, he returned to his hometown to find a way to retrieve his father's body for burial. Soon after, he learned that his father's kidnapping was actually due to his wife's brother, Zhang Rizhong, acting as an informant for the bandits. After Li returned to Nanjing, he specifically sent a letter to the local Public Security Bureau, instructing the Detective Team to strictly arrest and interrogate the suspect. Yesterday afternoon, Zhang was indeed captured on the Jiangbei bank of the South China Sea steamer. The suspect Zhang Rizhong has now been sent to the Public Security Bureau for verification and handling.

Representatives' Congress Telegraphed Request to Investigate Prosecutor: The Fifth All-County Representatives' Congress of Yin County believes that the prosecutor of the Yinxian District Court Prosecutor's Office, investigating the case of Yu Kangshu, the captain of the Ningbo Public Security Bureau Detective Team, executing the poor man He Shengtang, has been investigating for more than four months without concluding the investigation and filing a public prosecution. The handling is very inappropriate. The Representatives' Congress resolved (1) that the Congress telegraphed the Control Yuan to strictly handle the prosecutor in charge of this case and the captain of the Detective Team in accordance with Article 7 of the Impeachment Law; (2) that the Congress telegraphed the Provincial Executive Committee to send a letter to the Higher Court Prosecutor's Office to transfer jurisdiction of this case for prompt interrogation; (3) that the Congress telegraphed the Judicial Yuan to suspend the prosecutor handling this case from office for investigation. The Congress executed these resolutions last month. It is now learned that the Yin County Party Department received a reply telegram from the Judicial Yuan, the Administrative Department, which stated, "Qiaodai Telegram, has been issued to the Judicial Yuan for verification and handling. The Chief Prosecutor of the Zhejiang Higher Court has been ordered to send personnel to thoroughly investigate and verify the cause of He Shengtang's death and whether the handling of the prosecutor in charge of this case was inappropriate. It is expected that the truth of the case will soon come to light."

Pinghu 85

Various Industries Enthusiastically Help with Relief: The Pinghu County Fundraising Association for Relief of Flood Victims in Various Provinces convened local gentry and representatives of various agencies and groups at the Zhongshan Memorial Hall the other day to hold a meeting on relief for flood victims. It was resolved to borrow the Xinmin Theater for theatrical performances to raise funds. Those who voluntarily donated included the Pinghu Hotel Yanghe Teahouse, which will donate 50% of their profits for the next five days to help with relief. The Rice Industry Association also launched a fundraising campaign for flood relief, issuing donation books to solicit donations. The County Chamber of Commerce has also decided to donate 20% of the wages of all shop employees and workers in the county this month to help the disaster victims.

European Bees Damage Crops, Farmers Appeal: A bee farm in Hanmiao Town keeps 130 hives. Recently, when the rice crops were budding, the bees swarmed out and damaged many crops, causing great panic among the farmers. They immediately gathered the whole village to negotiate with the bee farm, but without result. Instructor Zhang of the Farmers' Association reported to the county government to send personnel to mediate. The farmers demanded that the bee hives be sealed, but the owner refused, resulting in a conflict. Three or four hundred farmers poured in and moved the bee hives. The Public Security Bureau Chief and police arrived to suppress the situation and issued a proclamation. The farmers also came to the city today (the 4th) to appeal to the County Party Department, the County Government, and the District Office.

Parricide Case Adjudicated: Lu Along, the parricidal son from Shiyantou outside the East Gate of Pinghu, was sentenced. He demanded silver from his father, Jin Chang, which led to the heinous crime. Along fled the scene and was later captured in Xinfeng Town, Jiaxing, and detained by the county government. On the morning of the 4th, Assessor Song summoned witnesses to hold a court hearing. After repeated interrogations by the assessor, the parricidal son Along, seeing that the witnesses had gathered and could not deny the facts, finally confessed. Assessor Song sentenced Lu Along to life imprisonment for the crime of manslaughter.

Huzhou 86

Machine Weaving Workers Petition Over Dispute: When silk sales were sluggish in Wuxing silk factories and independent machine weaving workers, employers reduced wages by one cent per foot. Now that the silk market sales are slightly better, workers are demanding that employers restore the original price. However, employers claim that silk sales are still sluggish due to the floods in various places and refuse to raise prices, leading to a county-wide strike by independent machine weaving workers. The Party and government agencies have repeatedly intervened to mediate, but the labor and management sides have each held their ground, making a resolution ineffective. On the afternoon of the 2nd, Party and government officials were discussing solutions at the County Party Department. Fearing accidents, they summoned the police team to maintain order. Around 6 PM, more than nine hundred machine weaving workers, unable to endure any longer, rushed into the County Party Department to petition. The police team stepped forward to stop them, leading to a conflict. Police officers fired several shots as a warning, injuring the head of worker Lu A'gen. The workers still gathered and did not disperse, arguing for a long time. General Manager Yan of the business community and Team Leader Wang of the Security Team came forward to persuade them, promising that labor and management would each send representatives to the County Chamber of Commerce on the 3rd for concrete consultations. The injured workers were sent to the hospital for treatment. The workers dispersed late at night.

Taizhou 87

Huge Debt Leads to Suicide by Hanging: Zhang Laoyi, a resident of Housi in Dongxiang, Linhai, squandered money on gambling and prostitution, accumulating huge debts that he could not repay. Overwhelmed, he hanged himself. His family discovered the body, but it was too late. He was already dead.

Education News

News Highlights

Salaries for Elementary School Teachers in the Eastern Provinces Special District 88

High monthly salaries and bonuses

The Ministry of Education, according to a report from the Education Department of the Eastern Provinces Special District, reports that elementary school teachers in the district are currently divided into four levels: Senior Head Teachers, with a monthly salary of 125 Harbin dollars (approximately $1.25 per current dollar); Senior Subject Teachers, with a monthly salary of $115; Junior Head Teachers, with a monthly salary of $105; and Junior Subject Teachers, with a monthly salary of $95. Teachers in outlying areas, who mostly live at the school, have salaries slightly lower than those in the local area. Senior Head Teachers receive a monthly salary of $110, with each lower level receiving $10 less. Teachers who have established schools on the original route, along with their families, receive free tickets for long-distance travel or are provided with housing. In terms of current compensation, it is not considered low compared to the interior. Regarding annual salary increases, the department has regulations for teacher incentives. Teachers who continue to work at a school for three years or more and have achieved results are eligible for a Level 1 bonus of $140. Teachers who have worked for two years or more and have achieved results are eligible for a Level 2 bonus of $120. Teachers who have worked for one year or more and have achieved results are eligible for a Level 3 bonus of $100. The Ministry of Education considers the salary situation and incentive regulations for elementary school teachers in the district to be generally appropriate and has approved the record.

Ministry of Education Explains Whether Education Association Executive Committee Directors Can Hold Concurrent Positions 89

Concurrent positions must not hinder association affairs

The Ministry of Education, according to a request from the Hunan Education Department to interpret whether Education Association Executive Committee Directors can hold concurrent positions, issued a directive stating that Article 24 of the Education Association Law stipulates that Education Directors, Directors, and Supervisors are all honorary positions. Concurrent positions are permissible as long as they do not interfere with association affairs. Please note and instruct compliance accordingly.

Fengyong Fushun Track and Field Contest 99

Yu Xihui's 1500 Meters

Breaks National Record Again

Just Four Minutes and Sixteen Point Four Seconds

Very Close to the Far East Record

Yu Xihui set a new national record of four minutes and sixteen point four seconds in the 1500 meters, which is very close to the Far East record. Zhou Lian's discus throw of thirty-four meters and twenty centimeters broke the North China record. (Note: The national record for 1500 meters is Jiang Yunlong's four minutes and twenty-three seconds, and the Far East record is Tsuda's four minutes and six seconds. The North China record for discus is thirty-three meters and sixty-four centimeters, and the national record is thirty-four meters and sixty-three centimeters.)

Local News

Xiong Xiling Proposes Four Methods to Raise Huge Disaster Relief Funds 113

Hoover Formally Approves Loan of American Wheat

The National Government's Disaster Relief Committee, in order to provide emergency relief for the Yangtze River floods, has not only requested the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to negotiate with American merchants for a loan of 15 million bushels of wheat, but also plans to issue 80 million in disaster relief bonds in the shortest possible time. It is now learned that with regard to the loan of American wheat, the committee received a report yesterday stating that the American President has now formally approved it. Regarding the issuance of 80 million in disaster relief bonds, the Beijing Red Swastika Society, fearing that it would be difficult to sell them all at once, has made a new proposal. They telegraphed committee members Zhu Qinglan and Xu Shiying, requesting them to consult with the Ministry of Finance. The two items of news obtained yesterday are recorded separately below.

▲American Approval Regarding the loan of American wheat, a foreign member of the committee received a report from the American side yesterday afternoon stating that American President Hoover had officially announced the previous day that he would agree to loan 15 million bushels of American wheat to China. Regarding the interest rate, it can be reduced from approximately 4.5% to 4%. However, the committee did not hold any meetings last night regarding this matter because the report was received late yesterday, and Minister of Finance Song had not yet returned to Shanghai.

▲Discussing Raising Huge Sums for Disaster Relief Yesterday, workgroup director Zhu Qinglan and others received a telegram from the Beijing Red Swastika Society, which read: "Generals Zhu and Chairman Xu, please note: We respectfully report that the great disaster has not ended, and the lower reaches of the Yangtze and Huai Rivers are again in danger. Alas, our people have been abandoned. Although the issuance of relief bonds has been decided, we fear it will be difficult to sell them all at once. We offer the following humble suggestions: (1) The Ministry of Finance should repay 14 types of domestic debt in September, totaling approximately 10,057,700 silver dollars. It seems possible to follow the old practice of only paying interest and postponing the repayment of principal for one year, and use this amount for disaster relief. (2) The British and German debts have been repaid. This customs revenue can be used to negotiate foreign loans from the United States, France, and other countries. (3) For countries with unsettled Boxer Indemnity funds, payments can be suspended for one or two years, as was done during the European War. For those with agreed uses, the budgeted silver funds in China will have surpluses due to the rising gold price, which can be negotiated with the Boxer Indemnity Committee members to be diverted to disaster relief. (4) In past disaster relief efforts, surcharges were levied on customs duties. This precedent can be used to negotiate with various envoys. If the Ministry of Finance agrees to the above four items, it should be possible to have 30 to 40 million dollars in cash available. Is this feasible? Please consider and decide. Xiong Xiling of the Swastika Headquarters bows and asks."

▲Request for Funds from the Beijing Shelter The National Government's Disaster Relief Committee: Minister Song's note: In response to the order from the Executive Yuan, the Capital City Flood Relief Association is approved to be dissolved. In the future, relief funds will be raised and allocated by the Disaster Relief Committee, and the relief and rehabilitation work will be handled by the Relief Affairs Committee together with the Nanjing Municipal Government. Upon receiving this order, the Capital City Disaster Relief Association was organized on the 3rd by personnel dispatched from this city to take over and continue the work. In addition to submitting a report, the original association had established three shelters. Due to the recent breaches of dikes and embankments in the suburbs, the number of disaster victims is increasing daily, with a total of over 35,000 people. At a cost of approximately five cents per person per day for half a pound of steamed buns, the monthly maintenance cost is estimated to be over 50,000 dollars. The funds transferred to the association amounted to only 2,000 dollars, which can only last for two days. Disaster victims from all over are continuously arriving in Beijing, and the situation is extremely urgent. We can only comply with the order and urgently request your committee to approve the advance allocation of 50,000 dollars to provide immediate relief. We urgently request that you remit the funds to Beijing by telegraph to provide relief. We eagerly await your order. The Nanjing Municipal Government Relief Affairs Committee respectfully requests. The committee replied by telegram: "To the Nanjing Relief Affairs Committee and the Municipal Government: We have just received your telegram. As there is an urgent need for funds to operate the disaster victim shelters, we approve the telegraphic transfer of 10,000 dollars from the Jin Cheng Bank tomorrow morning for urgent use. Please verify receipt and reply by telegram. The remaining funds will continue to be allocated by the Disaster Relief Committee."

City Chamber of Commerce Requests Use of Northeast Surplus Grain for Disaster Relief 114

Sending Disaster Victims to Reclaim Wasteland and Develop Border Regions

The City Chamber of Commerce telegraphed the Nanjing National Government and Zhang, Deputy Commander-in-Chief in Shenyang, requesting that the surplus grain from the Northeast be used for disaster relief. The original telegram read: (abbreviated titles) "This year's floods have affected as many as sixteen provinces. Supplementing the people's food supply to prevent disaster victims from dying is the most urgent task of the moment. Although the government has a proposal to loan wheat flour from the United States, the phased shipment to China will inevitably be too slow. It is better to seek domestically first, as the proximity will save provincial expenses, and the price will naturally be cheaper than purchasing from abroad. Moreover, no matter how hard we try to raise disaster relief funds, the vastness of the disaster area will inevitably be just a drop in the ocean. At this time, purchasing food, if possible, should prioritize domestic food supplies from areas with low prices. Arriving a day earlier means saving lives a day earlier. Saving a penny of expenses is equivalent to raising a penny of disaster relief funds. The advantages and disadvantages are obvious and need no further explanation. In the three northeastern provinces, except for the Liao River basin, which suffered from floods, all other areas have reported bumper harvests year after year. Surplus grain is piled up on the fields, leading to sluggish sales and goods being abandoned on the ground, resulting in the financial panic and industrial decline of the previous year. Recently, thousands of warehouses and tens of thousands of boxes of grain have been cheaply loaded and taken away by Soviet Russia, causing disaster victims in the southeast to lament that they have no way to buy grain. Is this not an abnormal phenomenon? According to reports, the Northeast has surplus grain of no less than 5 million tons. The stock is abundant and the price is low. From soybeans and sorghum to wheat flour and rice, everything is available. Rice is only nine cents per pound, and 100 pounds only cost nine dollars, which is cheaper than foreign rice. It is particularly suitable for sales. Moreover, the people in the sixteen provinces affected by the disaster do not all eat rice. Using coarse grains for disaster relief is a common practice throughout history. Soybeans and sorghum can all be used for disaster relief food and there is no need to worry about incompatibility. We should issue a clear order to use all the surplus grain from the Northeast at a fair price for disaster relief, allowing merchants to transport it freely. For maritime transport, transit tariffs should be waived. For land transport, railway freight rates should be greatly reduced. In such a shift, the Northeast will immediately see signs of commercial recovery, and the disaster areas will not have to worry about corpses on the roads. It is truly beneficial to both national welfare and people's livelihood. Furthermore, for famine victims from various provinces whose customs and habits are similar to those in the north and who are willing to go to Guanwai to make a living, the government or organizations should allocate funds for disaster relief to send them there in batches. This will be a long-term benefit for reclaiming wasteland and developing border regions. We respectfully offer our humble opinions and hope that you will adopt them. The Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce bows and sings."

Disaster Relief News from Various Provinces Yesterday 115

Cheng Jingsheng's Report on His Inspection Trip Back to Shanghai

Cheng Jingsheng, Director of the Jiangsu Flood Relief Association, established a resident office of the association in Zhenjiang and cooperated with the Jiangbei Flood Relief Temporary Relief Association, which was organized by Leng Yuqiu and Lu Xiaobo in Zhenjiang, to provide emergency relief to the victims in Gao, Shao, Ji, and the lower reaches of the river. Mr. Cheng personally went to Jiangbei to conduct a field survey of the disaster situation in various counties and the latest progress report on the relief work is excerpted below.

Summary Report on the Disaster Situation and Emergency Relief Work in Various Counties: The disaster area in Jiangbei is very wide. Gaoyou City, Shaobo Town, and the surrounding villages were the most severely affected. Shaobo, starting from the Six Gates, passing through Majia Gate, Dawang Temple, Jimaodai, the South Street of Shaobo Town, the north and south of Wanshou Palace, and ending at Zhaoguan Dam and Hehua Pond, had more than 20 breaches, ranging in width from ten to fifty or sixty zhang. More than half of the town's houses were destroyed. Rivers and lakes overflowed, creating a boundless expanse. The surrounding villages, such as Zhenwu Temple, Qiaoshu Town, Gongdao Bridge Fangjia Lane, and other remote small villages, which were located in low-lying areas, had all their houses submerged in water, suffering even more severely. Roofs and treetops became the areas where disaster victims fled for their lives, but their cries went unheard and rescue was not timely. The elderly and young were unable to climb and were swept away by the waves. The number of those who became victims of the water is difficult to estimate. Gaoyou’s Lujin Temple had a breach of more than 30 zhang to the south, 50 zhang to the north, 80 zhang at Twenty Li Pu, 40 zhang at Qigong Temple, 20 zhang at Yumatou, 50 zhang at Miaoxiang, and 80 zhang at Dangjunlou. The water force at Zhaoguan Dam and Dangjunlou was dangerous and the breaches were widening daily. If they are not repaired quickly, the consequences could be dire. The area outside the north gate is the commercial center and was the most prosperous. Now, it is a vast expanse of water, like a sea. The water is rushing and sounds like a bell. It flows eastward, and the sight is frightening. Although the city is fortunate not to have been completely submerged, the water depth has reached four or five feet and cannot be drained. Residents have fled to the city walls or climbed onto rooftops. Cooking fires have long been extinguished, and the water vapor is scorching. Even if they do not die in the flood now, it will be difficult to avoid dying from plague in the future. The vast countryside is several feet deep in water, and countless disaster victims are being swept away. The number of deaths in Gaoyou and Shao is extremely high. Floating corpses are seen in the waves, which is heartbreaking. Although there are no precise statistics, the number of casualties is said to be over 10,000. More than 10,000 who were rescued were sent to Yangzhou and Zhenjiang for shelter. This is the disaster situation in the upper reaches of the river. Since the dikes in Gaoyou and Shao broke, the Huai River has been flowing eastward, and the counties in the lower reaches of the river, such as Taizhou, Dongtai, and Xinghua, are the first to bear the brunt. The water level is rising daily, and cities and villages have mostly become swamps. The Taizhou Relief Association telegraphed that floating corpses have been seen in the countryside. Recently, they urgently telegraphed again, saying that two-thirds of the entire territory is submerged in water, and there are hundreds of thousands of disaster victims. Only more than 20,000 have been rescued so far, and the rest are still trapped in the water. The wind is strong and the water is rising, and rescue is extremely urgent. They requested that ships be dispatched quickly with food to provide relief. They also received a telegram from the leader of the third team of the Jiangbei Flood Relief Temporary Relief Association, saying that the disaster situation in Taizhou is extremely severe, and the food they brought is not enough to distribute. They urgently requested assistance. The Yun di dike in Dongtai collapsed, and the disaster situation is extremely severe. Telegrams for help were sent repeatedly. The magistrate of Rugao telegraphed that he has dispatched ships to assist and set up shelters. Xinghua is located in a low-lying area, and communication is cut off. The disaster situation can be imagined. In Zhenjiang County, Mashang Township and Gaozi Township in the second district, Tubin Township and Baolian Township in the fifth district, and Yulong Xin Zhou and Shunjiang Lao Zhou in the seventh district are all located along the Yangtze River. Recently, they have been affected by the impact of the river tides, and the dikes and embankments have collapsed. Houses, fields, and livestock have all been submerged, and tens of thousands of disaster victims are in a very miserable situation. According to the county magistrate and representatives of the disaster victims, letters and telegrams have been sent requesting assistance. Upon investigation, it was confirmed to be true. Funing, Rugao, and Taixing have all telegraphed about the disaster situation. Jiangning County’s Jiangxin Zhou and Jiangdu County’s Fogan Zhou and Zaixing Zhou have all breached their dikes and requested relief from the Jiangbei Flood Relief Temporary Relief Association and the resident office of this association. Personnel have been dispatched to investigate. However, the situation in Gaoyou and Shao was reported by Provincial Committee member Shi Zhiyun and National Flood Disaster Relief Committee member Jin Shude after personal inspections, which has been confirmed. Dongtai and Taixing have been repeatedly telegraphing for help in recent days. The disaster situation is expected to increase daily. A more accurate report will be submitted once the investigators return. This is the general disaster situation in various counties obtained in recent days.

Emergency relief in the disaster areas has been dispatched one after another by the Jiangbei Flood Relief Temporary Relief Association and the resident office of this association. As of September 1st, a total of five teams have been dispatched. The first team went to Xinghua and Dongtai, led by team leader Liu Yihang. The second team went to Gaoyou and Shao, led by team leader Zhou Zigeng. (On the day the dikes in Gaoyou and Shao broke, the Red Swastika Society dispatched members to lead ships to provide relief and telegraphed Yangzhou to send personnel to assist. More than 5,000 people were rescued. Zhou's trip was the third time disaster.) The third team went to Taixing and Dongtai, led by team leader Xu Xinshan. The fourth team went to Fanchuan, Xiaoji, and Zhouzhuang, led by team leader Yuan Xujiang. The fifth team went to Xinghua Shagou, led by team leader Tang Shiqing. Each team brought fourteen ships, tugboats, and more than twenty civilian boats, all carrying rice, noodles, sesame cakes, Jiang Guo Ba, Luo Gan brown sugar, ginger, straw paper, matches, candles, and epidemic prevention medicines to provide emergency relief. They were also instructed to hire small boats locally to go to the villages to find and rescue disaster victims and send them to various shelters. This is the general situation of the teams' departures in recent days. The disaster victims transported from the disaster areas to

The number of disaster victims in various shelters, including Yangzhou and Zhenjiang, has reached more than 10,000, and the number of disaster victims in Taixing has exceeded 20,000. Telegrams were sent to Nantong, Rugao, Taixing, and other counties to set up shelters, and the association provided funding. The replies from the governments of Tong, Rugao, and Taixing stated that they are rushing to handle the matter. However, due to the vast disaster area and the great distance between Xingdong, Gaoyou, and Shao, communication and the dispatch of ships to provide food were delayed. In order to expedite the response to the situation, it was decided to set up branch offices along the way in Yangzhou, Taixing, and the lower reaches of the river, and to invite one director and one deputy director to cooperate with local officials, gentry, and local organizations to handle the matter quickly and avoid delays. Five branch offices have been set up and are currently dispatching teams one after another, focusing on searching for disaster victims in various villages and planning for future plans. This is the general situation of the association's work in recent days. As for the actual situation in the disaster area, Yuqiu plans to go to investigate with Xiaobo in person in the near future. After returning to Zhenjiang, a more accurate report will be submitted.

Another report states that Cheng Jingsheng, Deputy Director of the Association, and temporary staff members Hu Junzhong and Hong, went to Gaobin and Shaobo in Jiangbei to conduct a field survey and returned to Shanghai at 5:00 PM yesterday. It is said that there is a very detailed report.

Zhu Qichen's Report on His Inspection of Disaster Relief in Wuhan 116

The Chinese Jisheng Association publicly appointed standing committee member Zhu Qichen to take charge of emergency relief in Wuhan. He traveled with many relief workers, carrying 60,000 dollars in relief funds, 10,000 bags of flour, and 40,000 bottles of relief medicine to investigate the details and provide effective relief. A letter has been received from Director Zhu, reporting that Qichen and his relief workers arrived in Hankou on August 26 and temporarily stayed in Room 40 of the Central Hotel, which served as a temporary office. The water in the room was more than three feet deep, and the foul air was unbearable. The mosquitoes were so numerous that it was difficult to sleep all night. Mosquito nets and mosquito coils were ineffective. Other locations were even more deeply submerged. Fortunately, the water and electricity companies and the water plant were well-protected, and there was no shortage of drinking water. However, the lights in the German and Japanese concessions were submerged and had long been plunged into darkness. It was impossible to enter and leave without a boat, and transportation was extremely difficult. Since the flooding of Hankou, the water depth is still more than ten feet in some places and several feet in others. There are ninety-eight shelters in Hankou, mostly run by charitable organizations, with varying sizes. For example, the Xinshichang Charitable Society can accommodate more than 3,000 people in each shelter, while smaller ones can only accommodate dozens of people. There are seventeen shelters in Wuchang, and Xiao runs a single shelter in Hanyang that can accommodate several thousand people. In terms of shelters alone, government funds account for about 30%. Before the Qingshan Dike broke, there were about 300,000 disaster victims. After the dike broke, the number increased by 200,000, for a total of about 500,000 disaster victims. This does not include those in other counties. They are currently living in the open air in Hongshan, Sheshan, Meizishan, Fenghuangshan, Guishan, and Heishan. Temporary thatched huts are being rushed to be built. Reed mats have been ordered from Shanghai, and wooden poles are being erected on the mountains to build thatched huts, which should be completed soon. The association plans to provide a portion of the food. Four relief workers have been sent to Dunrentang and other shelters in Hankou, totaling fourteen shelters, to begin an investigation. It is estimated that there are more than 3,000 refugees. We are working with Cai Fuqing, He Hengfu, and Wan Songtao to take over and provide flour, calculated for two months, which will cost about 20,000 dollars. The current disaster situation is serious and there are many refugees. Without urgently raising huge sums of money and preparing more cotton-padded clothing, it will not be enough to help in the future. This relief effort in Wuhan should be viewed with a long-term perspective. The Yangtze River basin is interconnected and its safety is related. If the disaster victims in Wuhan are rescued, the disasters in the downstream areas can be alleviated. It is hoped that charities in Shanghai will pay attention to this. According to the chairman of the Chamber of Commerce, He Hengfu and Huang Wenzhi, the disaster situation in Cai Dian in Hanyang is extremely severe. They plan to cooperate with the association and send people together to investigate before making a decision.

Standing Committee Meeting of the Emergency Relief Association 117

The Standing Committee of the Emergency Relief Association of Various Provinces held a temporary meeting at 4:00 PM yesterday. Chairman Xu Junren presided over the meeting. Qu Wenliu reported on the Baotang Dike Rescue Project. Yu Hongjun from the Municipal Government attended the meeting to discuss the situation. Mr. Yu was also present to describe everything in detail. Wang Xiaolai and Zhang Xiaolin proposed that the Baotang Dike Rescue Project was an urgent matter and that since the Municipal Government's Public Works Bureau was responsible for it, the Jiangsu Province should be telegraphed to immediately telegraph the 100,000 dollars originally planned for the provincial treasury to the Shanghai Municipal Government. The association would also assist with 50,000 dollars, which would be advanced by Mr. Zhang Xiaolin. It was estimated that another 50,000 dollars would be needed, which the Municipal Government would be responsible for raising. It was also requested that the Municipal Government be responsible for the repair of all important dike projects besides Baotang, such as Liuhe. This was unanimously approved. The Disaster Relief Bond Issue was discussed and it was resolved to send a telegram to the Executive Yuan, the Legislative Yuan, and the Ministry of Finance of the National Government, urging them to issue the bonds as soon as possible.

City Party Headquarters Issues Guidelines for Soliciting Donations for Disaster Relief 118

The city's Party member disaster relief donation teams, with designated team leaders and sub-team leaders appointed by the city Party headquarters, are actively proceeding with their work. The City Executive Committee yesterday also formulated a set of guidelines for soliciting donations for disaster relief and distributed them to the donation personnel for compliance. The second and third districts separately convened meetings with the branch team leaders to discuss the situation. The details are recorded as follows:

▲ Second District Team The second district Party branch sub-team leader, Wang Deyi, specially convened a meeting yesterday with the branch team leaders, including Wang Chunyuan of the 24th branch, Luo Lie of the 28th branch, Liu Jiwu of the 3rd branch, Mao Xiaxuan of the 18th branch, Wang Guan of the 11th branch, Yu Jinluo of the 22nd branch, Liu Yun of the 15th branch, Zhou Shuwang of the 2nd branch, Mei Guozhen of the 20th branch, and more than ten others. The sub-team leader reported on the disaster situation and the suffering of the victims in various places, saying, "Tens of millions of compatriots have been affected by the disaster and are in dire need of food. Disaster relief is like fighting a fire. I hope that all branch team leaders will quickly do their best to solicit donations." At the end, several methods of implementation were agreed upon. Starting today, donations will be solicited from all walks of life, and they will be concluded every two weeks and submitted to the City Party Headquarters for distribution.

▲ Third District Team The leader of the Party member disaster relief donation team of the third district Party headquarters of this city is Comrade Tang Liqing, an executive committee member of the district, appointed by the city Party committee. The branch team leaders are the standing committee members of each district branch. The district executive committee has already forwarded the order to its subordinates for guidance and has sent a letter to the district team leader to follow suit. The district team leader Tang has scheduled a meeting tomorrow (the 7th) at 1:00 PM to convene a discussion meeting with all branch team leaders (i.e., the standing committee members of each branch) to discuss implementation methods. The notice was issued yesterday.

▲ Key Points of Solicitation The guidelines for soliciting donations for disaster relief formulated by the City Executive Committee of this city are as follows: (1) Explain the extreme severity of this flood disaster. (2) Explain that this flood disaster requires assistance from individuals, society, and the nation. (3) Explain that Party comrades should especially rise up to help with disaster relief. This time, the heavy rains in the southeastern provinces have caused a disaster, with floods inundating the area, houses collapsing, and people and animals being drowned. The magnitude of the disaster is unbearable to witness. In Yutang, Hunan, thousands of people were swept away. The once prosperous three towns of Wuhan are now submerged. Other areas, such as the rice-producing areas of northern Anhui and the affluent areas of southern Jiangsu, are all a vast expanse of water without end. The mighty Yangtze and Han rivers are still surging. The vast lands of Yu are in danger of being submerged. The living have been reduced to starving people, and the disaster area is so vast that it spans almost the entire country, accounting for two-thirds of the national area. The number of victims is at least 50 million or more. This is truly a major change for the country and a strange disaster for the nation, which we cannot ignore in the slightest. Since the disaster is so severe, the disaster area is so large, and the number of victims is so numerous, relying solely on government relief is not only limited by financial resources but also may lead to neglecting one area for another. It is essential that the people of the whole country rise up together to overcome this great difficulty and carry out a movement to save people and save themselves. The people of Shanghai, in particular, have an undeniable responsibility. The reasons are as follows: 1. From the individual perspective, this flood disaster affects sixteen provinces, with five or six being severely affected and more than ten major cities and ports being hit. Shanghai is fortunate to have escaped this calamity. While our compatriots are trapped in the water, we are living in peace. Think of the 50 million compatriots in the Jianghuai and Hehan regions who have lost their homes and have no place to live, no clothes to keep warm, and no food to eat. They have no way to go to heaven and no way to enter the earth. Whenever we think of this tragic situation, we cannot help but shed tears. All our comrades and compatriots should have the heart to alleviate the hunger and suffering of others and do their best to fulfill their heavenly duty of helping those affected by the disaster. Moreover, Shanghai is a place where people from all over gather, and most are from various provinces. In addition to the relationship between compatriots, there is also the kinship of hometowns and villages. We should help them as fellow countrymen and as fellow villagers. Furthermore, Shanghai is the commercial center of the country, known for its strong financial resources, and extravagance prevails. The consumption of wine and food and the waste of luxury goods are countless every day. People from all walks of life should, in this time of great calamity, tighten their belts and save money to provide substantial assistance and set an example for the whole country. 2. From the social perspective, (A) if we cannot provide relief to the victims and ensure that they have food and shelter, then those who are left to die in ditches are extremely pitiful, and diseases and epidemics will spread endlessly, which is a great hidden danger for society. Not only that, but the victims who have lost their homes and jobs will seek a way to survive in all directions. If they cannot find a way to survive, they will be forced to take risks. A few will become thieves, and many will become bandits. They will kill and rob, or plot rebellion. Moreover, the communists in the country have not yet been completely wiped out, and they will inevitably tempt and incite the victims to take advantage of the situation and launch surprise attacks. Social order will be difficult to maintain, and the country will face a major disaster. 3. From the national perspective, our country's production is backward, and the economy cannot be self-sufficient. Now, the production functions and tools of sixteen provinces and regions have been destroyed, and the victims in the area cannot be saved. The country's food and other supplies will be completely exhausted, and the foundation of the social economy will be fundamentally shaken. The future of the country is unimaginable. As citizens, we should rush to the aid of the country and jointly seek to restore the order of the national economy. In summary, we know that we should all do our best to help with this flood disaster. As Party comrades, we bear the heavy responsibility of saving the country. At this time of national crisis, we should all do our best to contribute our intelligence and talent to the Party and the country. We should also contribute generously to the extent of our financial resources and provide practical assistance. We must know that every little bit helps, and every grain of sand can form a pagoda. This will not only benefit the disaster victims and give peace of mind but also benefit the foundation of the Party, the foundation of the country, and the livelihood of the society and the people. Executive Committee of the Shanghai Special City of the Chinese Nationalist Party
