Free Talk

Not Removing the Garden Grass - Casual Talks by Zhaifu

Easy to Kill, Difficult to Give Birth 167

Before a human life, there are parents; before parents, there are ancestors. Since the discovery of life on the Earth's crust eighty million years ago, it took seventy-six million years for mammals to appear, and then another three and a half million to five hundred thousand years for human form to emerge, enduring countless hardships. Having taken human form, countless more hardships from wild beasts, diseases, floods, droughts, and wars had to be endured for generations to survive and pass down to me. The brothers and sisters who were conceived at the same time as me numbered no less than a million, but only I was fortunate enough to enter the gate of life. If I had been born to an unwed mother, she could have aborted me, or thrown me into the river to drown after birth, or sent me to a foundling hospital, resulting in a living being entering and a dead one emerging. If I had been born into a poor family, hunger, cold, and illness would have been unavoidable, and in the event of natural or man-made disasters, children would have been exchanged for food. If I had been born into a wealthy family, then in warmth and satiety, I would have indulged in pleasure and died in comfort. If I had been born and lost my mother, or encountered a stepmother, then I would have been whipped and beaten day and night, how could I have survived? If I had been abducted by kidnappers, the girls would have been sold into brothels, and the boys would have been cut up and sold as meat-filled buns. If I had been born in a country without child labor protection, then machines would have been tigers devouring children. As for one difficulty after another, still able to progress from elementary school to middle school, there are only two or three hundred thousand out of four hundred million people. What are these two or three hundred thousand youths? They are the essence naturally selected over eight hundred thousand years. Now, the tens of thousands who are successful will sooner or later die in decadence; the tens of thousands who are unsuccessful will sooner or later die by the axe. How many are left? How difficult it is to give birth! How easy it is to kill!

Exchanging Paintings for Crabs by Qing Daoren 168

— Zheng Yimei

A prominent figure in Shanghai. Recently, the former disciples of Zeng and Li have organized to publish the works of both teachers. Which is a great thing. I recall that Qing Daoren was addicted to crabs, earning the title of "Li's Hundred Crabs." At that time, Daoren lived in Shanghai. The autumn wind was strong, and the purple crabs were freshly fattened. He wanted to feast, but his purse was empty. Helpless, he painted a hundred small crab paintings to satisfy his craving. The crabs were all painted in ink, without any color, yet the flavor was rich, a stroke of divine inspiration. His friend Feng Qiubai saw it and greatly appreciated it. He went to Suzhou to buy three large baskets of Yangcheng Lake golden-haired, round-bellied crabs as an exchange for the paintings. Qing Daoren was delighted to get the crabs and generously gave him all one hundred paintings. Qiubai then named his study "Hundred Crabs Studio" to show his appreciation. I heard that Qiubai crossed the sea to Taiwan last year to do business. I don't know if he brought these hundred crab paintings with him to a foreign land. Otherwise, they could be used to make engravings. Qing Daoren is known for his calligraphy, and painting is only a secondary pursuit. Years ago, the owner of Xinhange met Mr. Weng Yinruo, a famous calligrapher and painter, at an antique shop on Hulong Street in Wuzhong and saw one of Qing Daoren's short paintings. Yinruo praised it as a masterpiece. The owner of Xinhange exchanged it for five yuan and made it into a seven-character couplet. (Gao Bu Zheng Qi Han Wei Guo, Qi Wen He Yi Cai Zhonglang.) There was a title on the top (Jiyun.) The owner was not happy. He suddenly thought that my name was Jiyun, and gave me the couplet as a gift, saying, "Your name is Jiyun. This couplet must be written by you." I still hang it in my paper-screened, bronze-bottled room, longing for Yanyun, and am very grateful for the generous gift from the owner.

World Snippets 169

Unbreakable Glass: Westerners have a superstition that breaking glass brings seven years of bad luck. For many years, scientists have been trying to invent unbreakable glass. Recently, two young scientists at the Californian Institute of Technology in the United States have succeeded in inventing it. However, the manufacturing method is still kept secret. In Europe, a type of soft glass has also been made, mostly from vegetables. It looks just like real glass, but can be rolled up like paper and will not break if thrown or twisted.

▲Rewards for Cars Without Accidents In major cities around the world, cars are as numerous as clouds. Accidents and injuries are common. The Vienna Automobile Club in the Austrian capital, Vienna, has prepared many kinds of medals that can be attached to buttons or inserted on cars to reward general car drivers. The medals are also divided into grades. Those who have never had an accident or been fined in fifteen years get the first grade; ten years get the second grade; and five years get the third grade. People with cars generally feel honored to receive this award. (Overseas Guest)

Talks from a Returnee from Sichuan 170

— Chi Fo

The Shu province is located in the remote western frontier. Its mountains and rivers are dangerous and difficult. It is known as a land of silkworms. It has the danger of the Qutang Gorge in the east, the obstruction of the Jian Ge plank road in the north, borders Guizhou and Yunnan to the south, and connects to Kang and Tibet to the west. It is rich in products. The mountains are overlapping. It is indeed an area of four platforms, the country of heaven. Since history, it has been the place for heroes to establish dominance. By the end of the Qing Dynasty, the Sichuan Road Incident triggered the revolution, and the Qing Dynasty was overthrown. Zhao Erfeng and Duan Fang were both killed by the Sichuan people. When Xiangcheng was in power, he sent Wu Guangxin and Chen Huan to Sichuan one after another. Both failed and returned. Until now, it is still a situation of warlords occupying the land. The ancients said that the road to Shu is difficult, as difficult as ascending to the blue sky. I say that the governance of Shu is difficult, as difficult as ascending to the blue sky. Yesterday, at a friend's house, there was a guest who had returned from Chengdu. I inquired about the inside story of the Shu province. The guest sighed and said, "Bashu is a land beyond civilization. West of Yichang, as far as Chongqing, is Liu Xiang's territory. Chengdu is Liu Wenhui's sphere of influence. Northern Sichuan is Deng Xihou's base. Therefore, those of us who travel to Sichuan Province must pay taxes several times. In the autumn of the year before last, I passed through Wanxian. The inspection was extremely strict. I accidentally found two pairs of silk stockings in my suitcase. They wanted to levy taxes. I said that people cannot only prepare one pair of silk stockings. They must be able to change them. The inspector said angrily, 'Stockings can be bought in Sichuan. Why prepare two pairs? According to the law, taxes must be levied.' I had to pay it. The severity of the tax can be known. Until now, ironware and other items are strictly prohibited. It is said that iron is the raw material for manufacturing internal disturbances. The prohibition of iron is to curb the bud of chaos. All those who have a brigade or regiment of soldiers in Shu have more power than a king sitting on the south-facing throne. However, although Shu is divided into four, when foreign forces invade, they will quickly unite to resist foreign aggression, and they will shout the words '(the province is in danger)' to each other. Their spirit is no less than that of the Japanese in the east. Therefore, since the Republic of China, all those who have entered Shu have failed and returned. After the foreign forces have left, they will fight each other to compete for power. However, Yang Sen was quite knowledgeable in construction before he lost power. Today, the Chengdu Avenue is backed by mountains and faces the river. It is smooth and flat, and the scenery is beautiful, making people linger."

Memories of the Flood Relief 171

— Lü Bing

The flood in our country this time has spread to sixteen provinces. The suffering is severe. Newspapers have repeatedly reported it. There is no need to list them. However, the arrival of the flood is unpredictable. Even European countries that usually study flood prevention may not be able to completely avoid the disaster. Recently, in March of last year, a huge flood in southern France caused a disaster. The flooded area was as many as thirteen districts. At that time, the French president heard the news and personally went to the disaster area to express condolences and provide relief. The situation is the same as the current visit and inspection of Wuhan by Chairman Chiang. Now I will excerpt and translate some of the reports from European newspapers last year, so as to see the enthusiasm of the people in that country in rescue and protection. It may not be unhelpful as a lesson.

The rivers in southern France connect to the Mediterranean Sea and the Atlantic Ocean. In late February of last year, there was continuous rain. The speed of the water flow was like a galloping horse. In an instant, both banks rose sharply. The accumulated water was as deep as eight feet. According to residents of Moscow, the water rose to the second floor in just five minutes. At this time, the wireless stations in each district reported the flood. When the news spread to Paris, all the residents of the city were panicked and looked like a major disaster was imminent.

The people of France, in the midst of this turbulent wave, were also admirable for their relief measures. Within three days, all the Mather boats and paddle wheels near Batu, whether official or private, joined the rescue and relief of the disaster victims. In each district, there were about thousands of ships. The Paris Chamber of Commerce held an emergency meeting. In one day and night, the food and cash relief received from various places reached more than 50 million francs. The assistance from other cities was not included. It is estimated that the flood in France was largely restored to order in four weeks. The spirit of self-help is commendable. Now the flood in our country is waiting for relief. It is urgent. Saving people is to save ourselves. It is hoped that all sectors will actively donate.

Record of the Eight Section Exercise of Shaolin 172

— Li Xufan

The origin of boxing arts began at Shaolin Temple on Mount Song. It is said that during the reign of Emperor Wu of Liang, Dharma came east and resided on Mount Song, inventing the Yijin Jing and various sets of combat and legwork. Later, the best monks of the temple obtained his true teachings, passing them down through generations, establishing the Shaolin School and being regarded as its ancestor. His skills were superior to ancient animal arts. During the Song Dynasty, Emperor Zhao Kuangyin, the Great Ancestor, studied and comprehended these skills, advocating the teaching of combat arts, and thus there were classifications such as the Changquan School, the Chaquan School, the Hongquan School, the Huaquan School, and the Paoquan School. However, each had a set of Eight Section Exercise, each with different functions, capable of defeating enemies and beneficial for health. Therefore, Shaolin is the source of boxing arts, akin to the source of a river. Li Jixun of our Wu region is young and handsome, skilled in combat. In his childhood, he was taught by Ma Yushan, a judge of the Central Guoshu Institute, excelling in Shaolin Chaquan, and has long been renowned both north and south, a strong combat expert. Li entered the hall and chamber, and was well-educated, progressing so rapidly that he surpassed his master. Recently, he was hired by a school in this port. Some days ago, comrades welcomed him at Yepu Garden. After the wine was flowing, Li, at the request of his comrades, demonstrated a set of Shaolin Twenty-Four Histories, consisting of one hundred and eight moves, quite splendid. In the five aspects of hand, eye, body, footwork, he was thorough in all respects. His performance was accompanied by whizzing sounds. He then performed a set of Eight Section Exercise, which was particularly distinctive. Between his arm bones and joints, there were cracking sounds. His skin was as hard as iron. From beginning to end, he was invulnerable. I am an outsider, only seeing him as lively as a monkey, leaping into the air, not daring to add my own judgment. According to an expert, this Chaquan Eight Section Exercise has more and more difficult movements than other boxing arts. If one is not well-trained and profound, how can one reach this level of divinity? He can be said to be a rising star.

Casual Talks from the Di Xiang Zhai Studio 173

— Gan Yi

I once wrote Casual Talks from the Di Xiang Zhai Studio. My friend Shou Juan once published it in a bi-monthly magazine. Those who wanted to speak only revealed the tip of the iceberg. When I lived in the government office and was a Beijing official, I did not write for more than ten years. Now that I am at sea, Shou Juan asked me about it. I said, "Now is the time." So I continued to write it.

Rao Hanxiang

Some say that Rao Hanxiang was a disciple of Fan Zengxiang. After the Republic of China was established, he was hired by Li Yuanhong as the secretary of the E Military Government and the Minister of Civil Affairs. This has not been verified. Hanxiang was from Guangji, Hubei, not a disciple of Yunmen. Elderly figures in Hubei, such as Yang Xingwu (Shoujing), were superior to Yunmen in both learning and morality. There were many who were his teachers. Why must Hubei people be from Yunmen's lineage to have fame and reputation? This is not entirely true. When Hanxiang was not successful, he listened to the drums in Fujian as a salt commissioner, feeling depressed and frustrated. Yao Wenzhuo, the academic commissioner, read his poems and prose and was impressed, so he invited him to his home to teach his children. Because it did not freeze during the winter, Zhai Zhaoyan (Yueshan), the military commander in Hanhang, recommended him to a certain historiographer. Shan ordered him to draft a few official documents to determine his worth. Xiang completed it overnight. Shan laughed coldly after seeing the draft and said, "Is this enough to be my subordinate?" He was not hired. Xiang sighed when he heard the news. In the autumn of the Xinhai year, Huangpi established his teeth in Wuchang, first taking the recruitment of talent as a matter of utmost importance. At that time, many renowned scholars and celebrities gathered upon hearing the news. Xiang was then a clerk in the Department of Finance. He drafted a document, and the director threw it on the ground. Xiang could not bear it and wanted to leave. A certain elderly figure admired his talent and said to Huangpi, "At the beginning of the Republic, talent is hard to find. There is someone in Hubei like Lu Jingyu who is being wronged as a low-level official. He does not seek to be known, and people rarely know him. Why don't you recruit him for your own use? It is like Jin Gong to Changli." Huangpi was overjoyed and invited him into his tent with courtesy. Xiang often read the Xuan Gong Collection. The official documents he wrote were imitated and somewhat similar. Huangpi repeatedly drafted lengthy articles and sent them by telegram to the world. They were poignant and touching, and resonated with people. They were all things that the people of the world wanted to say but dared not say. As a result, the minds of the people of the country unconsciously turned to the area between the Yangtze and Han rivers. Huangpi's reputation gradually increased. Xiang was made the leader of his staff and recommended as the Director of Internal Affairs, and then promoted to Governor. Later, Huangpi was lured into the capital by Xiangcheng, staying in Xiaopenglai. Xiang also retired in frustration, only getting the name of Senator. When Huangpi was enthroned in the White House, Xiang was in charge of the Second Secretariat. After its director, Ding Foyan (Shiyi), left, he took over. He offended Huangpi with something. When Huangpi rose again, Xiang was unemployed. Jin Yongyan occasionally mentioned his poverty, saying that most of his old friends were high-ranking officials. Why does Jifeng not think of Miser Monk? Miser Monk was Xiang's courtesy name. Huangpi was moved and wrote the four characters "help manage the secretary" and showed them to Yongyan. Yongyan told Xiang about it. Xiang hurriedly went to see him. Huangpi refused because of illness. He insisted on asking to see him and finally got to see him. Xiang sobbed and said, "My parents gave me life, and the President kept me alive. Although the help is occasional and scattered, it is still inexhaustible." Huangpi smiled and said, "You have suffered with me for a long time. You were not involved in confidential matters. I know my mistake. You can wait." In less than three days, the order of the Secretary-General was issued. Huangpi said to Ha Hanzhang, "Did I want to wrong Miser Monk? I just wanted to blunt his sharp edge." Hu Jun Chaozong once told me the whole story. Chaozong was from Huangpi and served Huangpi with Xiang. His words should be credible. In the year of Yichou, Guo Songling's rebellion nearly killed Xiang. He said to others, "Songling once knelt down and begged him to draft an edict to condemn Zhang. I politely declined. Ling said angrily, 'How do you know that I will not be the head of state one day?' His words were sharp and satirical. I know his meaning. I joined the army in anger, not as fortunate as Lin Changmin." A year after Ling's rebellion, it was rumored that Zhang Hanqing (Xueliang) ordered his arrest. There was no such thing. Xiang was afraid and wrote a letter to Xueliang to clarify the falsehood, nearly ten thousand words. Zhang replied with a letter of comfort, also several thousand words. I made the draft by hand. Alas, those who are talented and frustrated should not worry themselves by looking at Hanxiang.

Novel Society

A Husband's Wife (6) 174

— Jiang Hongjiao

(But, at this time, we lock the gate!) The gatekeeper was hesitant. He knew that it was inappropriate to keep her outside the gate, but not locking the gate would hinder his duties.

(You just lock it. I'll wait for our master to come back.) Madam Li was a little angry.

She thought: Mr. Li is the head of the family, and everyone should wait for him.

(But, the alley gate should be locked at this time, Madam Li!) Because Madam Li gave the most rewards to each family in the neighborhood during the festival, the gatekeeper did not dare to be too negligent. He was still hesitant and told her the reason for locking the gate.

(Then wait a moment. Look, isn't there a rickshaw coming slowly over there? Maybe he's coming back.) She stared infatuatedly at the east. On the white, vast road, there seemed to be the shadow of a rickshaw. She was very happy, very eager, and unhesitatingly determined that the person in the rickshaw must be Mr. Li. But she was disappointed, and the gatekeeper was also disappointed. The rickshaw slowly, slowly, very slowly pulled to the entrance of the alley: but it didn't stop, it still pulled forward.

(What do you think? Mr. Li won't be back until three o'clock at the earliest. I've been opening the gate for a month now. It's windy and snowy outside, Madam Li, you should go back! I'll wait for you. When Mr. Li comes back, I'll accompany him to your front door. Don't worry! Let me lock the gate first, and then send Madam Li home, okay?) The gatekeeper asked Madam Li in half Shanghai dialect.

(No, just lock the gate! You go and sleep in the wooden shed. I'll wait here. When he comes back, I can call you to unlock the lock.)

(It's better to wait at home. Be careful not to catch a cold, Madam Li!) The gatekeeper said this, but he was already very impatient. He really pulled the iron gate shut and locked it.

She stood outside the iron gate, shivering and trembling, still staring infatuatedly at the distant and blurred eastern road, wondering if there were any figures or cars coming.

Commercial News

Financial Gold Prices Return to Lower Levels 175

▲Fell Six Taels Seven Yesterday, the benchmark gold price fell back, with a large fluctuation. From morning to noon, there were more than seven taels of reversals, which had broken through the 770 tael mark, but the result was a decline of more than six taels, due to the influence of the silver price conference. People are extremely panicked, but because the silver market has not changed, it opened slightly higher. After that, sellers rushed in and turned sharply lower, almost like a river flowing downhill. There were only one or two taels of reversals. As for foreign exchange, it seemed to be slightly looser, but at noon it fell to the border of 70 taels. The market is closed as usual on Saturday. Since the beginning of this week, the market has been quite strong, once breaking through the 80 tael mark, reaching 85 taels and eight cents. Afterwards, it hovered at a low peak, and finally reached 70 taels and two cents, a difference of 15 taels and six cents. The total decline compared to the end of last week was 11 taels and eight cents. There is likely to be a transformation in the future.

▲Opening Slightly Better This morning, the October opening was slightly higher by six cents, at 777 taels and five cents. There were no changes in the major news and the public or private telegrams regarding silver prices. US stocks fell slightly, but reports said that the International Silver Conference would be convened on September 17, which caused excitement. Generally, large accounts tend to sell, such as Yuanmao, Zhifeng, Yongbingxing, etc., causing the price to drop by more than one tael to 76 taels and one cent. Then it rose by a few cents to 7 taels. When the British gold announcement showed no change, it was 76 taels and three cents, but Yongfeng, Yuancheng, Yongtianfeng, Yongyiyu, etc. agreed to sell, and then dropped by two taels and a few cents, and at 10 o'clock it was 74 taels and two cents. Then, because the Japanese Bank absorbed the October British gold at 875, it rose by one tael to 75 taels and a half. Yarn and Cotton Yarn Market Decline Intensifies 180

The yarn market is trending weaker, and the decline is intensifying. The situation in overseas cotton yarn markets is consistently trending downwards, and the severe floods in all parts of China have caused a significant slowdown in sales, leading to increasing pessimism. Many small players are closing out positions, triggering the decline. However, most of the large bullish players remain unmoved. Most of the market is in a short position, but some large merchants are cautiously covering their positions, and the future situation is uncertain.

▲Man-made yarn futures decline by one to two taels. In the early market, buyers were scarce, and the market situation suddenly changed, with prices for all months falling by 0.2 to 0.5 taels. The cotton market is trending downwards due to continued declines in American cotton prices, easing gold prices, and persistent rain and wind in Shanghai, causing significant damage to cotton fields. However, the global cotton market is weak, and pressure from major players is increasing, making it difficult for the market to rise. However, most cotton merchants expect a poor harvest in China and are mostly in a bullish position. Therefore, based on the overall situation, both bullish and bearish sides have considerable strength, and the future situation is unpredictable.

Private Estimates of American Cotton 183

New York, 4th: The Fuxike Bureau's estimate for this year's new cotton crop is 66.6% of the normal annual production, totaling 14,718,000 bales. The previous estimate (August 6th) was 73.8% of the normal annual production, totaling 14,150,000 bales. The American Cotton Collection Office's estimate for this year's new cotton crop is 65.7% of the normal annual production, totaling 15,503,000 bales. The previous estimate (August 6th) was 70.6% of the normal annual production, totaling 13,451,000 bales.

Predictions from the American Cotton Government Report 184

New York, 4th: The second estimate of American cotton harvesting will be released on the 8th. Based on the average of various private estimates, the predicted production is 65.9% of the normal annual production, totaling 15,110,000 bales.

Last Week's American Cotton Decline Report 185

New York, 4th: A report on the cotton market for the past week states that the decline in cotton prices was due to favorable weather in the South, weakness in the grain and security markets, leading to renewed liquidation by bulls, and some new selling. Supply was absorbed by short covering and buying by fellow traders. The Louisiana legislature has passed a bill prohibiting cotton planting next season, with other states expected to take similar action, affecting approximately 75% of the total American cotton production. However, traders here doubt whether this measure will be effective. Southern sources report that cotton harvesting is significantly delayed, and farmers are selling less. It is also heard that cotton farmers are planning to hoard their cotton in the hope of achieving higher prices through relief measures.

Declining Trend in Starch Futures Market 190

Yesterday's starch market saw slightly better bids for foreign wheat in the morning by about 0.2 jiao, and prices for all months improved slightly due to the heavy autumn rain. However, the market atmosphere suddenly changed in the afternoon. The weather had cleared, and the arrival of foreign wheat in China was becoming a reality. A large factory had a large amount of foreign wheat and began selling heavily, reaching 600,000 to 700,000, causing panic and paralysis among those with bullish positions who could not support the market. Looking ahead, if actual sales do not improve, more changes may occur. As a result, this month's prices fell by 0.0175, October's by 0.0225, November's by 0.025, and December to February's by 0.0225.

Wheat Prices Continue to Fall 191

Yesterday's wheat market saw prices for all months rebound by 0.03 to 0.04 in the morning due to slightly better foreign wheat bids and the rain. However, the sharp decline in the afternoon was unexpected. A large factory was reported to have traded a large batch of foreign wheat, and the American relief wheat was certain to become a reality, leading to strong selling pressure. This situation was due to too many real goods, and the bullish position of inland guilds was also shaken. As a result, this month's prices fell by 0.05, October's by 0.04, November's by 0.04, December's by 0.05, January's by 0.06, and February's by 0.04.

Japanese Cocoons Transferred to Marseille 194

China Refuses to Use Japanese Goods, Stockpiled Cocoons Shipped Out in Batches

Japan's spring and summer cocoons this year had a good harvest. Given the severe shortage of cocoon production in China, and the reduction of import duties on Japanese cocoons, Japanese merchants have been shipping cocoons to Shanghai in large quantities, taking the opportunity to sell them. However, since Chinese manufacturers unanimously refused to purchase Japanese cocoons, the large batches of Japanese cocoons stored in Japanese post offices and foreign warehouses could only be sold through zero-sum sales. Therefore, in recent days, French postal exports have included Japanese cocoons being transferred to other countries. In the past half month, a total of three to four thousand bales of Japanese cocoons have been shipped out, with eight out of ten being shipped to Marseille and other ports in French territory.

Gongxi Green Tea Sales Brisk, Prices Rise 195

The market for Gongxi green tea from incoming tea factories showed a trend of development yesterday. The large Russian cooperative that distributes tea, seeing that British, Indian, and Chinese tea merchants were buying tirelessly and stocks were dwindling, telegraphed its Moscow headquarters for instructions, and prices rose sharply by two to three taels. Other goods, such as Zhenmei and Zhenmei needles, were scarce, and European sales were smooth. Chinese tea merchants took a firm stance, and market prices were rising without any fall.
